                              <abbr title="Tuesday, November 22, 2016 at 9:26am" data-utime="1479835580" data-shorten="1" class="_5ptz">

                   <div class="_5pbx userContent" data-ft='{"tn":"K"}'>
                    <div id="id_583f561e195e55814418897" class="text_exposed_root">
                     <p>
                      Friday, Dec. 2, 2-3pm in GQ Annex
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      &quot;The &#039;New&#039; Face of Italy: Towards a Policy of Inclusion?&quot;
                      <br />
                      Talk by Dr. Chiara Minestrelli, Visiting Scholar in Africana and Global Studies at Lehigh University.
                     </p>
                     <span class="text_exposed_hide">
                      ...
                     </span>
                     <div class="text_exposed_show">
                      <p>
                       Immigrants are changing the face of Italian culture, and yet the Italian media often portray stories of reticence, violence and segregation. The second generation of immigrants, born and raised in Italy, has been actively voicing their concerns with regard to their status as &quot;second-class&quot; citizens. Many have used music to address such concerns.
                      </p>
                      <p>
                       Dr. Minestrelli will address these topics, as well as that of the experiences of those Italians who choose to leave the country in search of a better future elsewhere.
                      </p>
                      <p>
                       Talk is free and open to the public. This event is sponsored by the Languages, Literatures &amp; Cultures Dept. and the Italian Studies Program.
                      </p>
                     </div>
                     <span class="text_exposed_hide">

                   <div class="_5pbx userContent" data-ft='{"tn":"K"}'>
                    <p>
                     An Italian academic offers advice to Americans eager to oppose Trump&#039;s initiatives: don&#039;t focus on his personality.  Focus on the issues...
                    </p>
                    <p>

                              Italy Approaches a Constitutional Reckoning
                             </a>
                            </div>
                            <div class="_6m7 _3bt9">
                             Italian Prime Minister Matteo Renzi had broad support for overhauling the country’s constitution, but now this pro-reform consensus has collapsed just four weeks ahead of a Dec. 4 referendum, Simon Nixon writes.

                    <div id="id_583f561e1a2223767028658" class="text_exposed_root">
                     <p>
                      Muhlenberg student, Cassie Seidel, has won the gold medal in couple&#039;s artistic roller skating at the World Championships in Novara, Italy.  I&#039;m not saying the studying Italian at Muhlenberg will necessarily get you a gold medal, but it doesn&#039;t hurt.
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Congratulazioni, Cassandra!
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="https://www.facebook.com/cassandra.seidel">
                       https://www.facebook.com/cassandra.seidel
                      </a>
                     </p>

                        <h5 class="_5pbw _5vra _11dd" data-ft='{"tn":"C"}'>
                         <span class="fwn fcg">
                          <span class="fwb fcg" data-ft='{"tn":"k"}'>
                           <a href="https://www.facebook.com/italianatmuhlenberg/?hc_ref=PAGES_TIMELINE&amp;fref=nf">
                            Italian Studies at Muhlenberg College
                           </a>
                          </span>
                         </span>
                        </h5>
                        <div class="_5pcp">
                         <span>
                          <span class="fsm fwn fcg">
                           <a class="_5pcq" href="/italianatmuhlenberg/photos/a.588231411327501.1073741828.588221351328507/693458180804823/?type=3" rel="theater" ajaxify="/italianatmuhlenberg/photos/a.588231411327501.1073741828.588221351328507/693458180804823/?type=3&amp;size=400%2C285&amp;fbid=693458180804823&amp;source=12&amp;player_origin=pages" target="">
                            <abbr title="Wednesday, September 28, 2016 at 2:46pm" data-utime="1475099205" data-shorten="1" class="_5ptz">

                              September 28
                             </span>
                            </abbr>

                         <span role="presentation" aria-hidden="true">

                         <a data-hover="tooltip" data-tooltip-content="Public" class="uiStreamPrivacy inlineBlock fbStreamPrivacy fbPrivacyAudienceIndicator _5pcq" aria-label="Public" href="#" role="button">

                 <div class="_5pbx userContent" data-ft='{"tn":"K"}'>
                  <p>
                   The French and Italian Clubs are organizing a trip for Muhlenberg students to see a Franco Zeffirelli production of Puccini&#039;s La Bohème at the Metropolitan Opera in NYC on Saturday, November 19 at 8 pm.
                  </p>
                  <p>
                   Cost: $30 (includes ticket and transportation). To reserve your spot, please pay the full amount to Dr. Chatzidimitriou (Ettinger 101C, Tuesdays and Thursdays from 12:30-2) by October 18th at the latest. First come, first served!
                  </p>
                 </div>

                  </p>

                     http://www.npr.org/podcasts/510310/npr-politics-podcast
                    </a>
                   </p>
                   <p>
                    NPR correspondent Ron Elving commenting on Democratic vice-presidential candidate Tim Kaine’s knowledge and use of Spanish:
                   </p>
                   <p>
                    “The thing that learning someone else&#039;s languages says is, ‘ultimate respect.’ There is nothing you can do that shows more respect for somebody else’s culture than to really work hard at learning the language. […] It is the ultimate sign of respect.”

                            A mafia expert has named &#039;the most corrupt country in the world&#039;
                           </a>
                          </div>
                          <div class="_6m7 _3bt9">
                           Britain is the most corrupt country in the world, according to journalist Roberto Saviano, who spent more than a decade exposing the criminal dealings of the Italian Mafia.
                          </div>
